          <td id="content">
           <article class="sc post-10207 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-butterflies category-butterfly-gardening-in-houston category-monarch-butterflies tag-cold-weather tag-freezing-temperatures tag-monarch-butterfly tag-survival" id="article-10207">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2016/03/24/how-cold-is-too-cold-for-monarch-butterflies/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to How Cold Is Too Cold For Monarch Butterflies?">
                  How Cold Is Too Cold For Monarch Butterflies?
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  March 24, 2016
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div id="fb-root">
               </div>
               <script src="http://connect.facebook.net/en_US/all.js#appId=20320310172&amp;xfbml=1">
               </script>
               <script language="JavaScript">
                FB.Event.subscribe('edge.create', function(response) {
 						_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','SocialSharing','Facebook - like button',unescape(String(response).replace(/\+/g, " "))]);
 					});
               </script>
               <script type="text/javascript">
                (function() {
 				    var po = document.createElement("script"); po.type = "text/javascript"; po.async = true;
 				    po.src = "https://apis.google.com/js/plusone.js";
 				    var s = document.getElementsByTagName("script")[0]; s.parentNode.insertBefore(po, s);
 				  })();
               </script>
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2016%2F03%2F24%2Fhow-cold-is-too-cold-for-monarch-butterflies%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                One of my more popular posts, at least in terms of comments, was the post titled
                <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2011/01/11/its-cold-can-monarchs-survive/" target="_blank">
                 “It’s cold, can Monarch’s survive.”
                </a>
                I listed a reference that said Monarch Butterflies can crawl at 41 degrees Fahrenheit, and can fly at 55 degrees Fahrenheit. I’ve said from my own experience the caterpillars can survive freezing temperatures, but not for long.
               </p>
               <p>
                If you’ve kept up with the Monarch populations that travel from Canada to Mexico to overwinter you already know that the population has been getting significantly smaller every year. However, this year, 2016, the Monarch’s overwintering in Mexico rose to 4.01 hectares compared to 1.13 hectares in the previous year (and even worse the year before that).  Sounds great right?
               </p>
               <p>
                Well bad news. The Monarch Butterfly population just can’t seem to get a break. On March 10-11, 2016 a severe winter storm struck the Monarch Sanctuaries (
                <a href="http://www.learner.org/jnorth/monarch/spring2016/08/monarch-butterfly-migration031116.html" target="_blank">
                 Storm Decimates Monarch Sanctuaries
                </a>
                ). The wind was blowing up to 60 miles per hour, it delivered 2.85 inches of rain, and worst of all, the temperatures dropped to 23.9 degrees Fahrenheit.
               </p>
               <p>
                At first, despite that severe storm, Mexico’s Environmental Protection Agency said “
                <a href="http://abcnews.go.com/International/wireStory/mexico-monarch-butterflies-survive-severe-cold-snap-37588688" target="_blank">
                 The monarch butterflies held up under the snowfall
                </a>
                .”
                <strong>
                 <span style="color: #ff0000;">
                  WRONG!
                 </span>
                </strong>
                Read about the real impact from those on the ground and not in the government,
                <a href="http://www.learner.org/jnorth/monarch/spring2016/09/c031516_impact.html" target="_blank">
                 Impact of the Storm
                </a>
                ,
                <a href="http://www.learner.org/jnorth/monarch/spring2016/09/c031516_pelon_sharp.html" target="_blank">
                 Observations from Cerro Pelon
                </a>
                ,
                <a href="http://www.learner.org/jnorth/monarch/spring2016/10/romero/romero032416.html" target="_blank">
                 A Sad Day in El Rosario by Estela Romero
                </a>
                and
                <a href="http://www.learner.org/jnorth/monarch/spring2016/10/brower032416.html" target="_blank">
                 Likely Storm Mortality in Mexico
                </a>
                . Look at these pictures posted by
                <a href="http://www.learner.org/jnorth/monarch/spring2016/10/romero/romero032416.html" target="_blank">
                 Estela Romero Pictures
                </a>
                . Dead Monarch Butterflies just cover the forest floor.
               </p>
               <p>
                Let me go over the main points of what I learned and the important part of this post. If Monarch Butterflies are exposed to rain (or wetness) at 24.08 degrees Fahrenheit, 50% of those will die. If they are wet and exposed to temperatures of 17.6 degrees Fahrenheit, then 100% will die. Monarch Butterflies fare a little bit better if they are not wet and experience cold temperatures. If they are dry, only 50% will die if temperatures are 17.6 degrees Fahrenheit (remember 100% if wet), and 100% will die if temperatures reach 5 degrees Fahrenheit and they are dry. My references for all this information is from
                <a href="http://www.learner.org/jnorth/monarch/spring2016/10/brower032416.html" target="_blank">
                 Likely Storm Mortality in Mexico
                </a>
                .
               </p>
               <p>
                In summary, things were starting to look a bit positive for the Monarch Butterflies this year where the population was at first estimated at 200 million. Then on March 10-11, a freak winter storm blew through the reserves with heavy rain, blistering winds, and freezing temperatures. This is literally right when the Monarchs prepare to leave the reserves and mate. It couldn’t have come at a worse time. Their fat reserves from hanging around in the trees all winter were at their lowest levels. Then the storm hits, and it’s estimated that 50% of the population died from that storm (100 million). So much for the good news:-(.
               </p>
               <div class="pp-fb-like-btn-wrap">
                <div class="fb-like" data-action="like" data-href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2016/03/24/how-cold-is-too-cold-for-monarch-butterflies/" data-layout="button" data-share="true" data-show-faces="false" data-width="95">
                </div>
               </div>

           <!-- #article-10207-->
           <article class="sc post-10197 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-dogs-pets category-german-shepherd-dog category-pets tag-dogs-pets tag-german-shepherd tag-golden-retriever tag-pets" id="article-10197">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2016/03/23/long-time-no-post/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to Long Time No Post">
                  Long Time No Post
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  March 23, 2016
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2016%2F03%2F23%2Flong-time-no-post%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                Hello everyone. I know it’s been a long time since I posted anything, a little over 1 year in fact. I have a couple of excuses, but none that are really that great, so I’ll just be honest. It seems like I’m making lots of posts about animals and wildlife and my pets on Facebook. I held off joining that thing as long as possible, but I finally did join about 1 year ago. The second reason is that it seems like I rarely use my professional camera lens, and I just run around with my iphone taking pictures.
               </p>
               <p>
                So anyway, let me share some news. My last post on February 23, 2015 was addressed to my previous German Shepherds veterinarians and my gratitude for the care they gave her. I still tear up a bit thinking about her, but I made a large poster of her and her life moment and that hangs in my room.  On August 16, 2015, my new German Shepherd puppy was born. Her name is Kaja which translates to Princess of Gods in Polish.
               </p>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10199" style="width: 810px">
                <img alt="Kaja as a puppy" class="size-medium wp-image-10199 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10199" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;Kaja as a puppy&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1443635193","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":"","orientation":"1"}' data-image-title="kaja puppy" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/kaja-puppy.jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/kaja-puppy-800x640.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/kaja-puppy.jpg" data-orig-size="1000,800" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2016/03/23/long-time-no-post/kaja-puppy/" height="619" id="10199" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/kaja-puppy-800x640(pp_w774_h619).jpg" title="kaja puppy" width="774"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Well this “little” puppy arrived at 8 weeks from the Czech Republic weighing 19 pounds. Sascha was 13 pounds at 8 weeks by way of comparison. Now this “little” puppy at just a hair over 7 months old is probably close to 85 pounds!
                </p>
               </div>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10200" style="width: 610px">
                <img alt="kaja march 2" class="size-medium wp-image-10200 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10200" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;kaja march 2&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"iPhone 6","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1456907492","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"32","shutter_speed":"0.00245098039216","title":"","orientation":"6"}' data-image-title="kaja march 2" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/kaja-march-2-e1458784988169-768x1024.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/kaja-march-2-e1458784988169-600x800.jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/kaja-march-2-e1458784988169-600x800.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/kaja-march-2-e1458784988169.jpg" data-orig-size="2448,3264" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2016/03/23/long-time-no-post/kaja-march-2/" height="800" id="10200" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="kaja march 2" width="600"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Again, comparing her to Sascha, I don’t think Sascha ever reached 85 pounds throughout her life. This dog is going to be huge! My Golden Retriever Maggie is still kicking at 14 years old. A little slower, not so great vision or hearing, but still the same ol’ happy dog.
                </p>
               </div>
               <p>
                <img alt="maggie upside down" class="size-medium wp-image-10201 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10201" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;maggie upside down&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"iPhone 6","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1458725492","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"1600","shutter_speed":"0.0666666666667","title":"","orientation":"6"}' data-image-title="maggie upside down" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/maggie-upside-down.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/maggie-upside-down-800x600(pp_w774_h580).jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/maggie-upside-down-800x600.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/maggie-upside-down.jpg" data-orig-size="3264,2448" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2016/03/23/long-time-no-post/maggie-upside-down/" height="580" id="10201" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="maggie upside down" width="774"/>
               </p>
               <p>
                <img alt="maggie looking at camera" class="size-medium wp-image-10202 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10202" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;maggie looking at camera&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"32","shutter_speed":"0.00194552529183","title":"","orientation":"6"}' data-image-title="maggie looking at camera" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/maggie-looking-at-camera-e1458785393241-768x1024.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/maggie-looking-at-camera-e1458785393241-600x800.jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/maggie-looking-at-camera-e1458785393241-600x800.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/maggie-looking-at-camera-e1458785393241.jpg" data-orig-size="2448,3264" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2016/03/23/long-time-no-post/maggie-looking-at-camera/" height="800" id="10202" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="maggie looking at camera" width="600"/>
               </p>
               <p>
                My backyard is still the wildlife paradise it’s always been. I probably have 100 or more Monarch caterpillars in my backyard right now. I have a ton of milkweed as each year the seeds disperse, and they have cleared my entire backyard of any milkweed leaves.
               </p>
               <p>
                My Purple Martin residents are in full swing right now and just started mating. I would expect them to start building their nests within the next week or so.
               </p>
               <p>
                Last, but not least, I have an Eastern Bluebird nest with 4 babies. As of today they are 11 days old and looking very healthy.
               </p>
               <p>
                So that’s the latest in a nutshell. Thanks for reading!:-)
               </p>
               <div class="pp-fb-like-btn-wrap">

                     I love your website.  I’ve been growing milkweed for only 2 years now and it’s become an obsession now.  I have at the least; thousands of monarch caterpillars and at 50+ hanging and getting ready to emerge.  I’m trying to grow more milkweed by the day to feed what is about to happen in my yard :).  I am located in Southern California where the weather is nearly perfect year round so no wonder they love it here.  Anyway, I just wanted to drop a line to say I love your site and am hooked on these beautiful butterflies.  I have lived on “Avenida Mariposa” which in Spanish means “street of the butterfly” for over 30 years, so it’s about time I took up this hobby.  And I too have large dogs.  Take care and thank you for your amazing site!
                     <span class="comment-time">

           <article class="sc post-10180 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-dogs-pets category-german-shepherd-dog category-personal-thoughts-and-questions category-pets tag-german-shepherd tag-pets" id="article-10180">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/02/23/dedication-and-appreciation-for-saschas-veterinarians/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to Dedication And Appreciation For Sascha’s Veterinarians">
                  Dedication And Appreciation For Sascha’s Veterinarians
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  February 23, 2015
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2015%2F02%2F23%2Fdedication-and-appreciation-for-saschas-veterinarians%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                I’m still mourning the loss of my German Shepherd Sascha, but I left work a little early for a couple of reasons. One, I wanted to donate Sascha’s leftover medications and food, as well as to give all her toys to a locally owned pet store.
               </p>
               <p>
                My purpose in this blog post is to formally state my extreme appreciation for Sascha’s veterinarians.  Sascha could have been treated just like “another dog” and I never felt she was. Granted, Sascha probably wouldn’t have allowed them to do that anyway because she loved going to the vet so much and was always on her best behavior.  Maybe I (Sascha) just got really lucky, but I hope any vet, or doctor will take a moment to remember why they entered their area of practice. It wasn’t for the money, it hopefully wasn’t for the prestige, it was because you had passion about what you would be doing. On every single visit that Sascha and I had, I always felt like each of you were right there with us, and I’m so appreciative of that.
               </p>
               <p>
                Sascha had vets at two (actually 3) different places. For dermatology, surgery, and internal medicine she went to
                <a href="http://www.gcvs.com/" target="_blank" title="Gulf Coast Veterinary Specialists">
                 Gulf Coast Veterinary Specialists
                </a>
                at 1111 West Loop South in Houston.  Two vets from there were very important in Sascha’s life and in case they ever happen to read this blog, I want them to know how special they were to me in providing care to her. First, is Dr. Suzanne Hunter (looks like she is no longer with Gulf Coast). Sascha had her spleen removed with Dr. Hunter, and her final emergency surgery was performed by Dr. Hunter. I never had the privilege of meeting Dr. Hunter while Sascha was alive, but she did make time for me today where I expressed my thanks for taking such good care of her both times.  There was also a Dr. Phipps that I met after Sascha’s final surgery and the day she passed. Dr. Phipps is an intern or a resident (I don’t know what they call it for a vet), but I’m sure I caused quite an emotional day when this big 6’1 guy comes in crying and hugging his dog who is dying. Thank you for spending the time with me in that room afterwards just to explain things to me and listen to my sadness.
               </p>
               <p>
                The other vet at GCVS I want to mention is
                <a href="http://www.gcvs.com/specialties/internal-medicine/internists" target="_blank" title="Gulf Coast Veterinary Internists">
                 Dr. Paul Manino.
                </a>
                He was Sascha’s internal medicine vet. He helped with her kidney issues, her spleen removal, and her compressed discs in her spine. He always explained things to me in ways that I could understand and I could just feel that he really cared about what was best for Sascha. Thank you as well Dr. Manino for meeting with me today.
               </p>
               <p>
                There’s another section of Gulf Coast that is located in a different location at 3800 Southwest Freeway, Suite 136. This is the location of
                <a href="http://www.gcvs.com/specialties/neurology" target="_blank" title="Gulf Coast Veterinary Neurologists">
                 Gulf Coast Veterinary Neurologists and Neurosurgeons
                </a>
                are located. After Sascha had her spleen removed and we were trying to figure out why she had some weakness in her back legs, I met
                <a href="http://www.gcvs.com/specialties/neurology/neurologists" target="_blank" title="Gulf Coast Veterinary Neurologists Dr. Giovanella">
                 Dr. Carley Giovanella
                </a>
                . Sascha and I had an extreme connection. She watched me like a hawk, and I her for that matter, and for a multitude of reasons, Dr. Giovanella was one of Sascha’s favorite vets.  I tear up when thinking about Dr. Giovanella I suppose because I always felt that she treated me like a human, not just a patient, and she treated Sascha as a very special dog, not just “a dog.” Dr. Giovanella was the first vet I went to visit today on my round of thanks, and she probably got the bulk of my tears and sadness. I’m so immensely grateful for the care you gave Sascha, and the compassion you showed me.
               </p>
               <p>
                Last, but not least is
                <a href="http://vitalpet.com/our_vets/" target="_blank" title="Dr. Warren Resell">
                 Dr. Warren Resell
                </a>
                at
                <a href="http://vitalpet.com/locations/atascocita-animal-hospital/" target="_blank" title="Atascocita Animal Hospital">
                 Atascocita Animal Hospital
                </a>
                . Dr. Resell is my primary vet for all of my animals so he was no stranger to Sascha. I was actually seeing Dr. Resell before I took Sascha to Gulf Coast for her emergency surgery. Once he saw the x-rays and had them read, he was the one who told me she needed emergency surgery. Like Dr. Giovanella, Dr. Resell was one of Sascha’s favorite vets. I’ve known Dr. Resell for years and he’s always answered every single annoying question I have asked, and even answered some before I asked. Dr. Resell has never been a vet that was okay, next patient, next, next, next. I know his staff has even had to remind him he had other appointments to attend to when he was spending time with me and one of my animals. Dr. Resell, I don’t know if you’re close to retiring, but please don’t. You’re my veterinary rock with all of my animals. I give them the love and compassion, but I need you to help me with their care. I know it’s selfish, and I’m sure there are lots of great vets around town, but Dr. Resell is a very special person to me and in the care of my animals. We also share a passion for birding. I dreaded telling you today about Sascha because I felt you really connected with her. Thank you for all the care you provided to her over her 11 years. I know she adored you.
               </p>
               <p>
                I’ve never been known for being short-winded, but please allow me to get a couple of items off my chest. I spent an extraordinary amount on Sascha’s veterinary care. I know many who would not do that, or could not afford to do that. For my animals I just try and provide the best care and the best lives they can absolutely have. It’s not about the money. I know a dog is a dog, a cat is a cat, and a bird is a bird. That’s just the thing though. My animals are not just dogs, cats, or birds. I give them all the love and compassion I can, and yes I’ve spent a ton on their veterinary care, but you know what? I would do it again. The love and compassion and financial resources I give and gave them is nothing compared to what they have given me. Animals, at least my animals, teach me compassion, kindness, understanding, and patience. There’s not a human being on this planet that could teach me what they have taught me (to be fair, I’m more likely to listen to an animal:-). The one thing about Sascha that I miss at this moment is how that dog would just stare at me with those big brown eyes. Her joys in life were to have a toy in her mouth, and to be around and watching me. For all of my flaws and imperfections, that dog adored me. How could I not use every resource I could to provide the best life I could for her.
               </p>
               <p>
                This post was supposed to be about Sascha and my appreciation for all of her veterinarians. It still is. Words don’t do justice to how I feel on the inside about the care that all of Sascha’s veterinarians gave her. I know Sascha will not forget you, and neither will I. Thank you!
               </p>
               <div class="pp-fb-like-btn-wrap">

           <article class="sc post-10177 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-blog-videos category-dogs-pets category-german-shepherd-dog category-personal-thoughts-and-questions category-pets" id="article-10177">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/02/21/i-lost-my-dog-sascha-today/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to I Lost My Dog Sascha Today">
                  I Lost My Dog Sascha Today
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  February 21, 2015
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2015%2F02%2F21%2Fi-lost-my-dog-sascha-today%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                I’m going to keep this brief, just because I’m so mentally and emotionally exhausted right this moment. I had to say goodbye to my 11 year old German Shepherd, Sascha.  In short, she had to have emergency surgery yesterday (Friday).  Got a call from the vet yesterday and today saying surgery went fine and she’s recovering. I went to visit her today at 11.  She was semi out of it, but she did raise her head to look at me and make eye contact.  At 2:30 I got another call from the vet saying Sascha was going downhill.  I asked if I could return.  At 2:45 I got another call saying things are really bad and she may be gone by the time I get there.
               </p>
               <p>
                Sascha being Sascha of course hung on until I got there. They suspected she was having numerous clots and the outlook wasn’t good regardless.  I said my goodbyes, as you can hear in the video, and thanked her for her wonderful companionship.  Shortly after I ended this video I heard her groan and said that’s enough. She’s hurting, please put her down.
               </p>
               <p>
                While they were euthanizing her I just kept saying, “it’s okay, you can go now, thank you, let go, it’s okay.”
               </p>
               <p>
                Obviously I’m grieving since this just happened a few hours ago, and her presence is all over the house with toys, food, medication, etc, so it’s tough.  I’ll write more in the next day or two.
               </p>
               <p>
                Sascha July 26, 2003 – February 21, 2015
               </p>
               <p>
               </p>
               <p>
                <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/Saschas-Goodbye.mov">
                 Saying Goodbye To My German Shepherd Dog
                </a>
               </p>

           <!-- #article-10177-->
           <article class="sc post-10173 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-butterflies category-butterfly-gardening-in-houston category-monarch-butterfly-caterpillars category-monarch-butterfly-chrysalis category-host-plants category-mexican-milkweed category-monarch-butterflies tag-mexican-milkweed tag-monarch-butterfly tag-monarch-caterpillar tag-chrysalis-monarch-butterflies" id="article-10173">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/16/raising-monarch-caterpillars-in-winter/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to Raising Monarch Caterpillars in Winter">
                  Raising Monarch Caterpillars in Winter
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  January 16, 2015
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2015%2F01%2F16%2Fraising-monarch-caterpillars-in-winter%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                Someone asked me to post an update to this since I made reference to it on Facebook.  A couple of weeks ago, until just yesterday, it has been very cold and rainy in Houston.  On a few of those days it was supposed to be below freezing so I moved my Milkweed plants to the garage, and all of the Monarch Butterfly Caterpillars indoors.
               </p>
               <p>
                Raising Monarch Caterpillars indoors is not difficult, provided you have enough Milkweed and to clean the cage you keep them in.
               </p>
               <p>
                Before I get to far, I have always assumed that extended temperatures below freezing would kill the Monarch Caterpillar. Perhaps that’s still true, but I can say with 100% certainty that one of my Caterpillars survived temperatures down to about 28 degrees with no problems.
               </p>
               <p>
                Here’s how I raise Monarch Caterpillars indoors. I have several of those plastic containers that you get at the pet store to house Hermit Crabs or whatever. Within that container I put a couple of twigs so that the Caterpillars can crawl to the top of the cage to form a Chrysalis, and also to balance some of the Milkweed so it’s just not piled on top of each other. I place a paper towel in the bottom to collect the frass (poop). I change the bottom of the cage every day or two, and add Milkweed as frequently as needed depending on the size of the Caterpillars and the quantity.  That’s it!  Below are 11 Chrysalises, and 2 remaining Monarch Caterpillars whom I hope will change to Chrysalis soon as I’m running out of Milkweed.
               </p>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10171" style="width: 810px">
                <img alt="Monarch Chrysalis on Plastic" class="wp-image-10171 size-medium ov-done" data-attachment-id="10171" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"iPhone 6","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1421440656","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"100","shutter_speed":"0.0333333333333","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="Monarch Chrysalis on Plastic" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Monarch-Chrysalis-on-Plastic.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Monarch-Chrysalis-on-Plastic-800x600(pp_w774_h580).jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Monarch-Chrysalis-on-Plastic-800x600.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Monarch-Chrysalis-on-Plastic.jpg" data-orig-size="3264,2448" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/16/raising-monarch-caterpillars-in-winter/monarch-chrysalis-on-plastic/" height="580" id="10171" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="Monarch Chrysalis on Plastic" width="774"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Monarch Chrysalises on Plastic Container Lid
                </p>
               </div>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10172" style="width: 610px">
                <img alt="Monarch Chrysalis on Twig" class="wp-image-10172 size-medium ov-done" data-attachment-id="10172" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"iPhone 6","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1421440678","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"80","shutter_speed":"0.0333333333333","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="Monarch Chrysalis on Twig" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Monarch-Chrysalis-on-Twig-768x1024.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Monarch-Chrysalis-on-Twig-600x800.jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Monarch-Chrysalis-on-Twig-600x800.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Monarch-Chrysalis-on-Twig.jpg" data-orig-size="2448,3264" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/16/raising-monarch-caterpillars-in-winter/monarch-chrysalis-on-twig/" height="800" id="10172" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="Monarch Chrysalis on Twig" width="600"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Monarch Chrysalis on Twig
                </p>
               </div>
               <p>
               </p>

           <!-- #article-10173-->
           <article class="sc post-10168 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-backyard-pond category-goldfish-pond tag-backyard-pond tag-butterflies-diseases tag-goldfish-pond" id="article-10168">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/16/goldfish-disease-identification-possible-tumors/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to Goldfish Disease Identification Possible Tumors">
                  Goldfish Disease Identification Possible Tumors
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  January 16, 2015
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2015%2F01%2F16%2Fgoldfish-disease-identification-possible-tumors%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                I did something exceedingly rare today because we had some rare weather. The sun was actually out today!  Finally.
               </p>
               <p>
                My original intent was just to replace the netting over the top of my pond. That turned into, well why not clean the pond. Five hours later I called it a day.
               </p>
               <p>
                Someone asked about an old post I did on Goldfish Diseases and if the disease was ever identified (it wasn’t). I responded to one of the comments saying this happens every year to a couple of my fancy goldfish. They do eventually die from whatever this is.
               </p>
               <p>
                Below is my pond with most of the water drained.
               </p>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10167" style="width: 810px">
                <img alt="Pond Cleaning 2015" class="size-medium wp-image-10167 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10167" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;Pond Cleaning 2015&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"iPhone 6","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1421421280","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"64","shutter_speed":"0.0333333333333","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="Pond Cleaning 2015" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/PondCleaning.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/PondCleaning-800x600(pp_w774_h580).jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/PondCleaning-800x600.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/PondCleaning.jpg" data-orig-size="3264,2448" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/16/goldfish-disease-identification-possible-tumors/pondcleaning/" height="580" id="10167" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="Pond Cleaning 2015" width="774"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Pond Cleaning 2015
                </p>
               </div>
               <p>
                These next 2 pictures are of one of the fancy goldfish that I captured to take a picture of. Those lumps on its body are consistent with what every sick goldfish has.  I’m not sure how many goldfish I have at this point, but I’m talking about perhaps 2 fish per year have this problem, always goldfish, never koi.
               </p>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10165" style="width: 810px">
                <img alt="Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill" class="size-medium wp-image-10165 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10165" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"iPhone 6","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1421420461","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"40","shutter_speed":"0.0166666666667","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Goldfish-Disease2.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Goldfish-Disease2-800x600(pp_w774_h580).jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Goldfish-Disease2-800x600.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Goldfish-Disease2.jpg" data-orig-size="3264,2448" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/16/goldfish-disease-identification-possible-tumors/goldfish-disease2/" height="580" id="10165" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill" width="774"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill
                </p>
               </div>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10166" style="width: 810px">
                <img alt="Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill Down View" class="size-medium wp-image-10166 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10166" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill Down View&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"iPhone 6","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1421420442","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"40","shutter_speed":"0.0166666666667","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill Down View" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/GoldfishDisease1.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/GoldfishDisease1-800x600(pp_w774_h580).jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/GoldfishDisease1-800x600.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/GoldfishDisease1.jpg" data-orig-size="3264,2448" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/16/goldfish-disease-identification-possible-tumors/goldfishdisease1/" height="580" id="10166" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill Down View" width="774"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Goldfish Disease on Head, Nose, and Gill Down View
                </p>
               </div>
               <p>
                Does anyone have any idea what this disease is? I saw references to a fungal infection, but I don’t think that’s it. I’m suspecting tumors, and according to
                <a class="broken_link" href="http://puregoldfish.com/goldfish-health/illness/" target="_blank" title="Goldfish Tumors">
                 this site
                </a>
                this is exactly what it appears to be.  There is no known treatment for tumors, and although it does suggest you can cut off the growths, with my luck I’d try that and have a dead fish in my hand.
               </p>
               <div class="pp-fb-like-btn-wrap">
                <div class="fb-like" data-action="like" data-href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/16/goldfish-disease-identification-possible-tumors/" data-layout="button" data-share="true" data-show-faces="false" data-width="95">
                </div>
               </div>
               <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled">

           <article class="sc post-10161 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-butterflies category-butterfly-gardening-in-houston category-monarch-butterfly-caterpillars category-monarch-butterflies tag-monarch-butterfly-caterpillars" id="article-10161">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/03/cold-weather-and-monarch-caterpillars/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to Cold Weather And Monarch Caterpillars">
                  Cold Weather And Monarch Caterpillars
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  January 3, 2015
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2015%2F01%2F03%2Fcold-weather-and-monarch-caterpillars%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                I was asked recently about Monarch Caterpillars and cold weather. Generally I have found that the caterpillars do just fine as long as it’s above freezing, but if it’s supposed to be below freezing I take some extra precautions.
               </p>
               <p>
                I have several of those small containers that you get at the pet store that house hermit crabs.  I simply cut off a few stems of milkweed and leaves, place those in the container along with the caterpillars.
               </p>
               <p>
                One thing you have to be prepared for once you bring them inside, is they will become much more active since they are no longer cold so make sure you have plenty of milkweed on hand.
               </p>
               <p>
                Here’s what my setup looks like
               </p>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10159" style="width: 810px">
                <img alt="Caterpillars in container up close" class="size-medium wp-image-10159 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10159" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;Caterpillars in container up close&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"iPhone 6","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1420285625","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"32","shutter_speed":"0.00833333333333","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="Caterpillars in container up close" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Caterpillars-in-container-up-close.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Caterpillars-in-container-up-close-800x600(pp_w774_h580).jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Caterpillars-in-container-up-close-800x600.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Caterpillars-in-container-up-close.jpg" data-orig-size="3264,2448" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/03/cold-weather-and-monarch-caterpillars/caterpillars-in-container-up-close/" height="580" id="10159" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="Caterpillars in container up close" width="774"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Caterpillars in container up close
                </p>
               </div>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10160" style="width: 610px">
                <img alt="Caterpillars in Container" class="size-medium wp-image-10160 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10160" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;Caterpillars in Container&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"2.2","credit":"","camera":"iPhone 6","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1420285651","copyright":"","focal_length":"4.15","iso":"32","shutter_speed":"0.0046511627907","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="Caterpillars in Container" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Caterpillars-in-Container-768x1024.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Caterpillars-in-Container-600x800.jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Caterpillars-in-Container-600x800.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Caterpillars-in-Container.jpg" data-orig-size="2448,3264" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2015/01/03/cold-weather-and-monarch-caterpillars/caterpillars-in-container/" height="800" id="10160" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="Caterpillars in Container" width="600"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Caterpillars in Container
                </p>
               </div>
               <div class="pp-fb-like-btn-wrap">

           <article class="sc post-10150 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-birds category-blue-dragonfly category-butterflies category-butterfly-gardening-in-houston category-camera-bodies category-camera-lenses category-canon-7d category-dragon-and-damselflies category-ef-300-f2-8 category-giant-swallowtails category-gulf-fritillary category-hummingbird-bush category-insects category-nectar-plants category-photography category-ruby-throated-hummingbird category-wildflowers category-wildlife category-zinnia tag-bird-photography-in-texas tag-butterfly-gardening-in-texas tag-dragonflies tag-gulf-fritillary-butterfly tag-ruby-throated-hummingbird" id="article-10150">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2014/09/08/butterflies-dragonflies-and-hummingbirds-getting-nectar/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to Butterflies, Dragonflies And Hummingbirds Getting Nectar">
                  Butterflies, Dragonflies And Hummingbirds Getting Nectar
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  September 8, 2014
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2014%2F09%2F08%2Fbutterflies-dragonflies-and-hummingbirds-getting-nectar%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                I’m a little tired tonight, but not much detail is needed. Pulled out the camera again, and despite the horrendous afternoon light, took some pictures of Ruby Throated Hummingbirds, Dragonflies, and Gulf Fritillary Butterflies, and a Giant Swallowtail Butterfly laying eggs on my Lemon Tree.
               </p>
               <p>
                Can you find the Male Ruby Throated Hummingbird in the picture below?
               </p>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10146" style="width: 810px">

                  <div class="comment even thread-even depth-1 sc pp-comment" id="comment-32813">
                   <div class="comment-text">
                    <p>
                     <span class="comment-author">
                      <a class="url" href="http://fireflyfisherman.blogspot.com" rel="external nofollow">
                       Justin
                      </a>
                      <span>
                       -
                      </span>
                     </span>
                     This time of year is great. The migration has started and the flowers are buzzing with life. Our butterflies and hummingbirds are going nuts and all the butterfly weed and fennel has been eaten down to just the stalks. Hope you have a wonderful migration through your area.
                     <span class="comment-time">
                      September 10, 2014 – 9:04 am
                     </span>
                    </p>
                   </div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="comment byuser comment-author-texdr bypostauthor odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 sc pp-comment last-comment" id="comment-32839">
                   <div class="comment-text">
                    <p>
                     <span class="comment-author">
                      <a class="url" href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com" rel="external nofollow">
                       texdr
                      </a>
                      <span>
                       -
                      </span>
                     </span>
                     The hummers are picking up every day. I really enjoy watching them, and having them buzz around. Lots of males were here yesterday, and I could swear there were a couple of female today. I’m sure I’ll be getting lots of pictures and videos this weekend
                     <span class="comment-time">
                      September 10, 2014 – 8:47 pm
                     </span>
                    </p>
                   </div>
                  </div>

                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2014/09/01/butterflies-dogs-lizards-and-hummers/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to Butterflies, Dogs, Lizards, and Hummers">
                  Butterflies, Dogs, Lizards, and Hummers
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  September 1, 2014
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">

                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">

               <p>
                I’m back after a long hiatus. I finally decided to pick up the camera again, after using my iPhone to take just random shots. The afternoon light was horrendous, but I still had fun.
               </p>

           <article class="sc post-10093 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-birds category-purple-martin category-wildlife tag-bird-photography-in-texas tag-birds tag-eggs tag-nesting tag-purple-martin" id="article-10093">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2014/05/10/purple-martin-egg-laying-update-for-may-10-2014/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to Purple Martin Egg Laying Update For May 10 2014">
                  Purple Martin Egg Laying Update For May 10 2014
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  May 10, 2014
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2014%2F05%2F10%2Fpurple-martin-egg-laying-update-for-may-10-2014%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                Decided to do a Saturday morning check on the 2 Purple Martin houses I have.  Previously I counted 60 eggs. This time I counted 73 eggs.  It looks like it’s going to be a very busy year for the parents.  A couple of the nests have 7 eggs. On those nests, those parents really have to work hard to keep those babies fed.  So far we’ve had a relatively good year in terms of rain, and the temperatures have certainly been lower. Hopefully the can hunt down lots of dragonflies when those babies start getting really hungry!
               </p>
               <p>
                Below are the current nest and egg counts
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 20 – 7 eggs (was 6)
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 25 – 5 eggs (was zero)
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 5 – 5 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 3 – 4 eggs (was 2)
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 4 – 6 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 8 – 6 eggs (was 5)
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 6 – 6 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 7 – 6 eggs (was 5)
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 11 – 5 eggs (was 4)
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 9 – 7 eggs (was 6)
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 10 – 6 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 12 – 6 eggs (was 5)
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 2 – 5 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 1 – 0 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Total = 73 eggs (was 60)
               </p>
               <div class="pp-fb-like-btn-wrap">

                </div>

           <article class="sc post-10089 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-dogs-pets category-german-shepherd-dog category-personal-thoughts-and-questions tag-cancer tag-dogs-pets tag-german-shepherd tag-pets" id="article-10089">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2014/05/04/german-shepherd-day-9-after-spleen-removal-miracles-happen/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to German Shepherd Day 9 After Spleen Removal: Miracles Happen">
                  German Shepherd Day 9 After Spleen Removal: Miracles Happen
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  May 4, 2014
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2014%2F05%2F04%2Fgerman-shepherd-day-9-after-spleen-removal-miracles-happen%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                I first got the call from the vet surgeon on Thursday. I think she said something like, “well, we got the pathology results back for Sascha.” I had prepared myself mentally for just about anything the vet would tell me, except for what she actually told me.
               </p>
               <p>
                Sascha did NOT have cancer and Sascha does NOT have cancer. The tumors in her spleen were not cancerous tumors.  “Excuse me, what?”
               </p>
               <p>
                Sascha did not have cancer and does not have cancer. It’s very unusual (I can’t remember if she said they have never seen it, or rarely seen it), but Sascha’s tumors in her spleen were the result of a blood infection, not cancer.
               </p>
               <p>
                Let me back up a bit and re-describe my meeting with the internal medicine vet on the day of surgery.  Sascha had at least 3 very large tumors in her spleen. In all likelihood it is cancer. In 75% of cases of tumors in the spleen the cancer has normally spread to other organs. In about 25% of cases the cancer is contained just in the spleen.  I’m sure he said of course there are some unusual circumstances, but that’s how my brain translated the information.
               </p>
               <p>
                Thus, Sascha’s results were extremely rare, and quite frankly, there could not have been a better outcome.  I’ve been asked by a couple of people was it even necessary for her spleen to be removed. Absolutely!  The spleen was enlarged, and had at least 3 very large tumors inside. The chance of the spleen rupturing and Sascha bleeding internally was very high.
               </p>
               <p>
                So what about the 2-6 months time frame that Sascha was expected to live? Well, I think you can throw those numbers out the window. Assuming we can treat the blood infection with antibiotics, Sascha should be just fine. She still has the spinal nerve degeneration, which I wasn’t even considering treating because I didn’t expect her to live long enough.
               </p>
               <p>
                And, if you’re curious about how Sascha is doing and feeling, I can tell you she is acting completely normal, just like she was before all the medical events. She constantly has a toy in her mouth, digs in the trash to eat paper towels, occasionally barks while in her crate just to annoy me, and loves to snack on an occasional piece of dog poo when I’m not paying attention:-). Frankly, I don’t care what she does anymore, I’m just happy she will likely be around for a little while longer. She gets her staples out on Tuesday so I should have more information to share at that time.
               </p>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10085" style="width: 610px">
                <img alt="Sascha Day 9 After Spleen Removal" class="size-full wp-image-10085 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10085" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;Sascha Day 9 After Spleen Removal&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"\u00a9 Lawrence Mayran, Ph.D.","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":""}' data-image-title="Sascha Day 9 After Spleen Removal" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/wpid10084-Sascha-day-9.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/wpid10084-Sascha-day-9.jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/wpid10084-Sascha-day-9.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/wpid10084-Sascha-day-9.jpg" data-orig-size="600,800" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2014/05/04/german-shepherd-day-9-after-spleen-removal-miracles-happen/wpid10084-sascha-day-9-jpg/" height="800" id="10085" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="Sascha Day 9 After Spleen Removal" width="600"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 Sascha Day 9 After Spleen Removal
                </p>
               </div>

           <article class="sc post-10086 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-birds category-photography category-purple-martin category-wildlife tag-bird-photography-in-texas tag-birds tag-nesting tag-purple-martin" id="article-10086">
            <div class="article-wrap sc content-bg">
             <div class="article-wrap-inner">
              <div class="article-header normal" data-role="header">
               <div class="article-title-wrap">
                <h2 class="article-title">
                 <a href="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2014/05/04/first-purple-martin-eggs-of-2014/" rel="bookmark" title="Permalink to First Purple Martin Eggs of 2014">
                  First Purple Martin Eggs of 2014
                 </a>
                </h2>
               </div>
               <div class="article-meta article-meta-top">
                <span class="article-date article-meta-item">
                 <span>
                  May 4, 2014
                 </span>
                </span>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="article-content sc" data-role="content">
               <div class="trackable_sharing">
                <a href="" onclick="_trackableshare_window = window.open(this.href,'share','menubar=0,resizable=1,width=,height='); _trackableshare_window.focus(); return false;" style="text-decoration: none; white-space: nowrap;" target="_blank" title="">
                 <img alt="" class="ov-done" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/plugins/trackable-social-share-icons/buttons/f4//.png" height="0" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" width="0"/>
                </a>
                <br/>
                <div style="padding: 5px 0 0;">
                 <fb:like font="" href="http%3A%2F%2Fwww.butterfliesandwildlife.com%2F2014%2F05%2F04%2Ffirst-purple-martin-eggs-of-2014%2F" send="true" show_faces="true" width="450">
                 </fb:like>
                </div>
                <br/>
                <g:plusone annotation="bubble">
                </g:plusone>
               </div>
               <p>
                I decided to do a nest check today in all of my Purple Martin houses, and I hit the jackpot.  I’m just including one picture just so you can get an idea.  All told, there are 60 eggs so far in twelve different rooms.  I’m sure some of the counts will go up, especially in the nests that just have 2 or 4 eggs.
               </p>
               <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_10083" style="width: 810px">
                <img alt="First Purple Martin Eggs of 2014" class="size-full wp-image-10083 ov-done" data-attachment-id="10083" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="&lt;p&gt;First Purple Martin Eggs of 2014&lt;/p&gt;
 " data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"\u00a9 Lawrence Mayran, Ph.D.","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":""}' data-image-title="First Purple Martin Eggs of 2014" data-large-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/wpid10082-First-Martin-eggs-of-2014.jpg" data-lazyload-src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/wpid10082-First-Martin-eggs-of-2014(pp_w774_h580).jpg" data-medium-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/wpid10082-First-Martin-eggs-of-2014.jpg" data-orig-file="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/wpid10082-First-Martin-eggs-of-2014.jpg" data-orig-size="800,600" data-permalink="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/2014/05/04/first-purple-martin-eggs-of-2014/wpid10082-first-martin-eggs-of-2014-jpg/" height="580" id="10083" src="http://www.butterfliesandwildlife.com/wp-content/themes/prophoto4/images/blank.gif" title="First Purple Martin Eggs of 2014" width="774"/>
                <p class="wp-caption-text">
                 First Purple Martin Eggs of 2014
                </p>
               </div>
               <p>
                Nest 20 – 6 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 5 – 5 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 3 – 2 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 4 – 6 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 8 – 5 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 6 – 6 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 7 – 5 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 11 – 4 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 9 – 6 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 10 – 6 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 12 – 5 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Nest 2 – 5 eggs
               </p>
               <p>
                Total = 60 eggs
               </p>
               <div class="pp-fb-like-btn-wrap">
